Introduction:
The Iranian nation declares its commitment to human rights as set forth in the Universal Declaration of Human Rights adopted in Paris in 1948.

ğŸ”¹Article 1

Iran is a democratic, non-sectarian, and socially equitable republic. The republic guarantees the equality of all citizens before the law, without discrimination based on family origin, race, gender, or religion

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 3:54â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Article 2

The official language of the Iranian Republic is Persian (and English...). The national emblem is a tricolor flag of green, white, and red (with a symbol in the middle) or without a symbol. The national anthem is [unknown]. The motto of the republic is "Freedom and Equality". Its foundation is based on "government of the people, by the people, and for the people."

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 3:54â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Article 3

National sovereignty belongs to the people, who exercise it through their representatives and by means of universal suffrage. No portion of the people nor any individual may arrogate to themselves this right.

Voting by direct or indirect suffrage, under conditions laid down by the Constitution, is guaranteed to all citizens of Iran, regardless of gender, upon reaching the legal age, and who are possessed of the necessary qualifications as determined by law.

All citizens of Iran, both men and women, who have reached the age of majority and are possessed of the necessary civil and political rights, as determined by law, have the right to participate in elections under conditions laid down by law.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 3:54â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Principle 4

Political parties and groups compete in elections. Their formation and activities are free, and they are obligated to uphold the principles of national sovereignty and democracy.

ğŸ”¹ Principle Five

The President of the Republic ensures the observance of the Constitution. With his/her oversight, he/she guarantees the regular functioning of public authorities and the continuity of the government. The President is responsible for safeguarding national independence, territorial integrity, and the observance of international treaties.

ğŸ”¹Seventh Principle (of the Iranian Constitution)

The President is elected by an absolute majority of votes. In the event that no candidate receives an absolute majority of the votes in the first round, a second round is held on the following Friday, between the two candidates who received the highest number of votes in the first round.

The voting begins at the invitation of the government. The new President must be elected at least forty days and no more than sixty days before the end of the term of the incumbent President.

In the event of the absence of the President for any reason, or with the approval of his/her excuse by the Constitutional Council and the approval of an absolute majority of its members, who shall convene upon the invitation of the government, the temporary duties of the President shall be assumed by the Speaker of the Senate, except in cases provided for in Principles 11 and 12 of this law. If the Speaker of the Senate is also excused from carrying out these duties, the government shall assume responsibility for them.
In the event of the absence of the President or when the Constitutional Council definitively declares the President's excuse, the election of a new President shall be held at least twenty days and no more than thirty-five days after the vacancy, unless the Constitutional Council declares a state of emergency.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 3:55â€¯PM]
If, during the seven days preceding the deadline for the introduction of Presidential candidates, a person who has announced his/her candidacy no later than sixty days before that date dies or becomes incapacitated, the Constitutional Council shall decide on the postponement of the elections.

If one of the candidates dies or becomes incapacitated before the first round, the Constitutional Council shall announce the postponement of the elections.

If one of the two candidates who received the highest votes in the first round dies or becomes incapacitated, the Constitutional Council shall announce the postponement of the second round, and new candidates shall be introduced in accordance with the regulations.

Ø¨Ù‡ Ù¾ÛŒØ´Ù†Ù‡Ø§Ø¯ Ù†Ø®Ø³Øª ÙˆØ²ÛŒØ±ØŒ Ø§Ø¹Ø¶Ø§ÛŒ Ø¯ÛŒÚ¯Ø± Ø¯ÙˆÙ„Øª Ø±Ø§ Ù†ØµØ¨ ÙˆØ¹Ø²Ù„ Ù…ÛŒ Ù†Ù…Ø§ÛŒØ¯.
Article 8:

The President appoints the Prime Minister. In case the Prime Minister tenders the resignation of the government, the President concludes his duties.

Upon the proposal of the Prime Minister, the President appoints and dismisses other members of the government.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 3:55â€¯PM]

The President is the head of the Council of Ministers.

ğŸ”¹Article 10

The President signs and issues the law within fifteen days after its adoption by the government. He can request Parliament to review the entire law or some of its provisions before the expiration of this period. Parliament cannot reject this request.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 3:56â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Article 11

At the suggestion of the government during parliamentary sessions or at the joint proposal of the two houses of parliament published in the official newspaper, the President can submit any bill related to the organization of public powers, reforms related to the country's economic or social policies, reforms related to public services involved in these policies, or approval of a treaty that will not adversely affect the performance of institutions, to a referendum.
When a referendum is held at the government's suggestion, the government delivers a speech to each of the houses, and negotiations take place after the speech.
If a referendum leads to the approval of a bill, the President signs the law within fifteen days after the announcement of the election results and issues an executive order for its implementation.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 3:56â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ Article 12

The President, after consulting with the Prime Minister and the Speakers of the Parliament, may declare the dissolution of the National Assembly.
General elections are held at least twenty days and no later than forty days after the dissolution.
The National Assembly is legally formed on the second Friday after the elections. If this session is held outside the regular session period, a special session will be held for a period of fifteen days. The dissolution of the National Assembly is not permitted in the year following these elections.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 3:56â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ Article 13

The President signs the guidelines and regulations approved by the Council of Ministers.
He appoints military and national officials.
The government's advisors, the secretary of the Society for the Award of Honors, ambassadors and extraordinary envoys, advisors to the Court of Accounts, governors, senior officers and heads of academies, and managers of central offices are appointed to the Council of Ministers.
The fundamental law defines other professions that are appointed by the Council of Ministers and the conditions under which the power of appointment for national and military professions can be delegated to another person to be executed in the name of the President.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 5:30â€¯PM]

Article 14:

The granting of credentials to the ambassadors and extraordinary envoys to foreign countries is the responsibility of the President. The President also accepts the credentials of ambassadors and extraordinary envoys from foreign countries.

ğŸ”¹Article 16

Whenever the Republic's territorial integrity, national independence, or international commitments are seriously threatened, and the regular performance of the aforementioned public powers in the Constitution is disrupted, the President shall take necessary measures, after official consultation with the Prime Minister, the heads of the legislative bodies, and the head of the Constitutional Council, to remedy the situation.

The President shall inform the public of the situation through an announcement.
These measures must be taken in a manner that enables the aforementioned public powers in the Constitution to carry out their duties in the shortest possible time. In this regard, the President shall consult with the Constitutional Council and call for a parliamentary session to address the issue.
The National Assembly cannot be dissolved during the exercise of these extraordinary powers.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 5:31â€¯PM]

The President has the right to grant amnesty

ğŸ”¹Article 18

The President's communication with the parliamentary assemblies shall be made through a message that shall be read out to the assembly and shall not be open to discussion. For this purpose, a special session of the assembly may be convened outside the period of its ordinary sessions.

ğŸ”¹ Article 19

Except for cases provided for in Articles 8 (paragraph 1), 11, 12, 16, 18, 54, 56, and 61 of the Constitution, the President's orders must be co-signed by the Prime Minister and, if necessary, by the responsible ministers, in addition to the President's signature.

ğŸ”¹ Article 20

The government determines and directs the country's policies. Governmental agencies and the military are under the government's control.
The government is responsible to the parliament according to the conditions and procedures set forth in articles 49 and 50.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:17â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 21

The administration of government affairs and the responsibility of national defense are with the Prime Minister. They ensure the enforcement of laws. Except for the cases specified in Article 13, the Prime Minister has the authority to enact regulations and appoints national and military officials.
The Prime Minister can delegate some of their powers to the ministers.
If necessary, the Prime Minister substitutes for the President in chairing councils and committees provided for in Article 15.
The Prime Minister, exceptionally and by express delegation, may preside over the Council of Ministers instead of the President for a specific session.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:17â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 22

The opinions of the Prime Minister, if necessary, are approved by the responsible ministers for implementation.

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 23

The duties of government members are incompatible with representation in parliament or trade union representation at the national level, as well as with holding government jobs or any other professional activity that conflicts with these duties.
The Constitution defines the conditions under which the successors of such duties, jobs or representations are replaced.
The replacement of parliamentary members is carried out in accordance with Article 25.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:17â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 24

The parliament consists of the National Assembly and the Senate.
Members of the National Assembly are elected by direct vote.
Members of the Senate are elected by indirect vote and guarantee representation of the provinces and regions of the country. Iranians residing abroad have representatives in the Senate.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:17â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 25

The parliament consists of the National Assembly and the Senate. Members of the National Assembly are elected by direct vote. Members of the Senate are elected by indirect vote and represent the constituencies and regions of the country. Iranian nationals residing outside Iran also have representatives in the Senate.

The constitution specifies the duration of the parliament's term, the number of its members and their rights, the conditions of their election, cases of disqualification and conflict of interest. It also specifies the conditions for filling vacancies in the event of a seat becoming vacant, and individuals are invited to replace the members or senators until the next general or partial elections of the parliament to which they belong.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:17â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 26

No member of the parliament can be pursued, arrested, detained or tried for their opinions or votes expressed during the discharge of their duties. No member of the parliament can be arrested or subjected to any other restriction or deprivation of liberty during the parliamentary term, in criminal or misdemeanor cases, without the permission of the parliament to which they belong. However, in the case of a flagrant crime or conviction, this permission is not required.

If requested by the parliament to which the member belongs, the detention, restrictive or punitive measures against them shall be suspended during the legislative term.

The relevant parliament is legally required to hold extra sessions to ensure the implementation of the above provision, if necessary.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:17â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 27

Any mandatory proxy is invalid.
The right to vote belongs exclusively to the individuals who are members of the parliament.
An organizational law may permit representation of a vote in exceptional cases. In this case, no one can accept more than one proxy vote.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:17â€¯PM]

Article 28:

The parliament shall convene in an ordinary session on the first working day of Mehr month and shall end on the last working day of Khordad month, in accordance with the law.

The number of days that each parliament may hold sessions during the ordinary session shall not exceed one hundred and twenty days. The weeks during which each parliament holds sessions shall be determined by that parliament.

After consultation with the interested parties, the Prime Minister may decide, with the consent of the majority of the members of each parliament, to hold additional sessions.

The days and hours of the sessions shall be determined by the rules of each parliament.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:18â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 29

At the request of the Prime Minister or a majority of members of the National Assembly, the Parliament may convene an extraordinary session with a specific agenda.

When an extraordinary session is convened at the request of members of the National Assembly, the Parliament shall issue an order to that effect as soon as it convenes the session, and no later than twelve days after the session is formed.

Only the Prime Minister can request the convening of a new extraordinary session before one month has passed since the date of the order to end the previous session.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:18â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 30

Except for cases where the Parliament convenes an extraordinary session by law, an extraordinary session shall be opened and closed by order of the President.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:18â€¯PM]

Ù‚ÙˆØ§Ù†ÛŒÙ† Ø¨Ø±Ù†Ø§Ù…Ù‡ØŒ Ø§Ù‡Ø¯Ø§Ù Ø§Ù‚Ø¯Ø§Ù…Ø§Øª Ø§Ù‚ØªØµØ§Ø¯ÛŒ Ùˆ Ø§Ø¬ØªÙ…Ø§Ø¹ÛŒ Ø¯ÙˆÙ„Øª Ø±Ø§ ØªØ¹ÛŒÛŒÙ† Ù…ÛŒÙƒÙ†Ø¯.
Ù…ÙØ§Ø¯ Ø§ØµÙ„ Ø­Ø§Ø¶Ø± ØªÙˆØ³Ø· Ù‚Ø§Ù†ÙˆÙ† Ø¨Ù†ÛŒØ§Ø¯ÛŒ Ø¨Ù‡ Ø·ÙˆØ± Ø¯Ù‚ÛŒÙ‚ ØªØ¹ÛŒÛŒÙ† Ùˆ ØªÙƒÙ…ÛŒÙ„ Ù…ÛŒØ´ÙˆØ¯.
Article 34:

Laws shall be passed by the parliament.

Provisions relating to the following matters shall be determined by law:

Civil rights and basic guarantees granted to citizens for enjoying public freedoms; people's compliance in personal and financial affairs with the national defense system.
Nationality, personal status and qualification, marital system, inheritance and endowment monopolies.
Definition and determination of crimes and offenses and the penalties imposed thereon; criminal procedure rules, amnesty and pardon, establishment of new hierarchies of courts, judges' regulations.
Sources, rates, and methods of collecting various taxes and the system of coinage and banknote printing.
The law also determines the provisions relating to the following matters:

The electoral system for parliamentary and local councils.
Establishment of various public institutions.
Basic guarantees granted to state and military employees.
Nationalization of institutions and the transfer of ownership of institutions from the public sector to the private sector.
The law specifies the fundamental principles concerning the following matters:

The overall organization of national defense;
Local government, its powers, and resources;
Education;
The system of ownership, property rights, and civil and commercial obligations;
Labor rights, trade union rights, and social security.
Financial laws shall be enacted subject to conditions specified by the fundamental law for government revenues and expenditures.
Planning laws shall determine the goals of the government's economic and social actions.

The provisions of this article are determined and completed in detail by the fundamental law.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:36â€¯PM]

Article 35:

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 37

Issues that are not within the scope of the law are regulated by regulations. Texts that have a legal form and have been issued on these matters can be changed by decree after consultation with the Cabinet, provided that they do not violate the Constitution.

Laws that are enacted after the promulgation of the Constitution cannot be changed by decree, unless the Constitutional Council declares that they are within the scope of regulations according to the previous paragraph.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:37â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 38

The government can obtain permission from the parliament to make decisions for a limited period of time through "directives" that are usually within the scope of the law for the implementation of its program. These directives, after obtaining the opinion of the Council of Ministers, will be adopted by the cabinet and will gain executive power after publication. However, if a draft law regarding their approval is not presented to the parliament until the date specified in the law granting powers, the said draft law will not be considered.

After the expiration of the period mentioned in the first paragraph of this article, the directives are unchangeable, except by law and in matters within the scope of the legislative branch's powers.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:37â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 39

The Prime Minister and the Members of Parliament simultaneously propose laws.
After obtaining the opinion of the Council of Ministers, draft laws are discussed and reviewed in the Council of Ministers and then presented to the office of one of the two houses of Parliament. Financial budget bills are first presented to the National Assembly.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:37â€¯PM]

Article 40:

Proposals and amendments presented by members of Parliament, if approved, should not result in a decrease in public income or an increase in public expenses, and should not be acceptable.

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 41

If it becomes clear during the parliamentary review that a proposal or amendment is not within the scope of the law or contrary to the authority granted by Article 38, the government can refrain from accepting it. In case of disagreement between the government and the relevant parliament, the Constitutional Council will decide within eight days at the request of one of the parties.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:52â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 42

Discussion about legislative bills begins in the first chamber to which the bill has been referred by the government. A chamber that receives a passed bill from the other chamber discusses and examines it.

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 43

At the request of the government or the receiving parliament, bills and legislative proposals are sent to special committees formed for this purpose to be reviewed. For bills and proposals that have not been requested in this regard, they are sent to one of the six permanent committees in each parliament.

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 44

Members of Parliament and the government have the right to propose amendments.
After the start of the negotiations, the government can object to any amendment that has not been previously submitted to the commission.
If requested by the government, the Majlis expresses its opinion on all or part of the text under discussion in a single vote, taking into account the proposed or accepted amendments by the government.

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 45

All bills and legal proposals are reviewed sequentially in both houses of parliament in order to approve a similar text. If a bill or legal proposal fails to pass after two rounds of voting in each of the houses due to lack of agreement, or if the government declares urgency, the Prime Minister is authorized to form a joint commission of members from both houses in equal numbers. The commission is required to propose a text on the remaining regulations under discussion.

The government presents the text prepared by the joint commission for approval to both houses. No amendment is accepted without the government's agreement.

If the joint commission fails to approve a unified text or if the text does not pass according to the conditions specified in the previous paragraph, the government can request the National Assembly to make a definitive decision regarding the above-mentioned text after a re-examination. In this case, the National Assembly can discuss the text prepared by the joint commission or the latest text that it has voted on, and the Senate can make amendments if necessary.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:53â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 46

Laws that are granted the status of fundamental laws by the Constitution are approved or amended under the following conditions:
The first chamber can only consider a bill or legislative proposal for voting and approval after fifteen days have passed since receiving it.
The procedure mentioned in Article 45 can be implemented in this regard. However, in the event of disagreement between the two chambers, the text is only approved by an absolute majority of the votes in the National Assembly's final vote.
Fundamental laws related to the Senate must be approved in the same way in both chambers.
Fundamental laws can only be signed and enforced as an order when the Constitutional Council has declared them in accordance with the Constitution.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:53â€¯PM]

Article 47:

The Parliament approves financial bills under conditions provided for by a fundamental law.
If the National Assembly fails to express its views within forty days of receiving a bill, the Government informs the Senate and the latter must make a decision on the bill within 15 days. The subsequent steps shall be carried out in accordance with the conditions provided for by Article 45.
If the Parliament fails to express its views within 70 days, the provisions of the bill can be enforced through the necessary executive orders.

If the budget bill that determines the revenues and expenditures of a period is not presented in due time to be endorsed before the beginning of that period, the Government urgently requests the Parliament to grant it permission to receive taxes and ensures the approved service credits through an executive order.
The duration provided for in this article shall be suspended when Parliament is in recess.
The Court of Audit supervises the Parliament and the Government in the implementation of financial laws.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:54â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 48

Without any damage to the implementation of the last three clauses of Article 28, the agenda of the parliament includes discussions about government legislative proposals and bills presented by parliament members, in accordance with the precedence and order determined by the government.

One weekly session is allocated to questions from parliament members and government responses, in accordance with the precedence.

One monthly session is allocated to the agenda set by each parliament, in accordance with the precedence.

Ù†Ø®Ø³Øª ÙˆØ²ÛŒØ± Ø§Ø®ØªÛŒØ§Ø± Ø¢Ù† Ø±Ø§ Ø¯Ø§Ø±Ø¯ÙƒÙ‡ Ø§Ø² Ø³Ù†Ø§ Ø¯Ø±Ø®ÙˆØ§Ø³Øª ØªØ§ÛŒÛŒØ¯ Ø³ÛŒØ§Ø³Øª ÙƒÙ„ÛŒ Ø±Ø§ Ù†Ù…Ø§ÛŒØ¯.
ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 49

The Prime Minister, after obtaining the vote of confidence from the Council of Ministers, accepts responsibility for the government's programs or possibly general policies in front of the parliament.

The National Assembly can challenge the government's responsibility by approving a motion of censure. Such a proposal can only be received with the signatures of at least one-tenth of the members of the National Assembly. The vote takes place 48 hours after the submission of the motion of censure. Only the favorable votes are counted, and the censure is approved only with the majority of the members' votes. Except for the cases provided for in the following paragraph, a representative cannot sign more than three censures during a regular session and more than one censure during an extraordinary session.

The Prime Minister can, after the decision of the Council of Ministers, hold the government accountable for the approval of a specific text in front of the National Assembly. In this case, the approved text is considered, unless a motion of censure is approved within 24 hours of its submission, according to the conditions provided for in the previous paragraph.

The Prime Minister has the right to request a vote of confidence from the Senate on general policies.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 6:54â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 50

When the National Assembly approves a proposal for impeachment or rejects a government plan or policy, the Prime Minister must tender the resignation of the government to the President.

Article 51:

In case of necessity for the implementation of Article 49, all regular and extraordinary sessions shall be postponed by law. For this purpose, complementary sessions shall be held.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 7:20â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸ Article 52

The negotiation of treaties and the signing of them is the responsibility of the President. He shall be informed of negotiations for the conclusion of an international agreement that do not require his signature.

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 53

Treaties of peace, treaties of commerce, and treaties or agreements concerning international organizations, as well as those which entail a financial commitment on the part of the State or affect the public rights shall be concluded only by virtue of a law. They shall not be valid until after ratification or approval.

Any relinquishment, exchange, or transfer of territories without the approval of the people concerned is not valid.

**Article 53 (1)
The Republic may conclude agreements with other states which are committed to similar obligations regarding asylum and protection of human rights and fundamental freedoms. Such agreements shall determine the competence of the respective governments to examine applications for asylum presented to them.

Even if an application for asylum does not fall within the competence of the governments referred to in the first paragraph of this article, authorities of the Republic shall always grant asylum to any foreign national who, due to his/her activities in favor of freedom, has been subjected to persecution, or to any applicant for protection who seeks Iran's support for such reasons.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 7:21â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 54

If the Constitutional Council, at the request of the President, the Prime Minister, the President of either of the two Houses of Parliament, or sixty members of the National Assembly or sixty senators, declares that an international commitment contains a provision contrary to the Constitution, the authorization to ratify or approve such commitment may only be given or such commitment may only be approved after the Constitution has been revised.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 7:22â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 55

Treaties or agreements duly ratified or approved shall, upon publication, prevail over domestic laws, provided that such treaties or agreements are implemented by the other party.

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 56

The Constitutional Council is composed of nine members, whose terms of office are six years and are not renewable. Every three years, one third of the members of the Constitutional Council are replaced. Three members are appointed by the President of the Republic, three members by the President of the National Assembly, and three members by the President of the Senate.

In addition to the nine members mentioned above, former Presidents of the Republic shall be members of the Constitutional Council by virtue of their office throughout their lifetime.

The President of the Republic appoints the President of the Constitutional Council. In case of a tie, the President of the Constitutional Council has the casting vote.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 7:30â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ï¸Article 57

Membership in the Constitutional Council is incompatible with holding ministerial office or membership in Parliament. Other incompatibilities shall be determined by fundamental law.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 7:30â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Article 58

The Constitutional Council monitors the proper implementation of the presidential election law. This council addresses objections and announces the election results.

ğŸ”¹Article 61

Basic laws, before being signed and issued as executive orders, as well as internal regulations of the National Assembly before implementation, must be referred to the Constitutional Council for its opinion on their conformity with the Constitution.

To this end, laws may also be referred to the Constitutional Council by the President, Prime Minister, Speaker of the National Assembly, Speaker of the Senate, or sixty representatives or senators, before being signed and issued as executive orders.

In the cases envisaged in the above two paragraphs, the Constitutional Council must give its opinion on the matter within one month. However, in case of urgency, the aforementioned period shall be reduced to eight days at the request of the government.

In such cases, the referral to the Constitutional Council suspends the deadline.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 8:59â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Article 62

Regulations that are deemed contrary to the Constitution cannot be signed or issued as executive orders.

Decisions of the Constitutional Council are not subject to objection, and their implementation is necessary for public authorities and administrative and judicial officials.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 8:59â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Article 63

The regulations related to the organization and functioning of the Constitutional Council, the methods of handling cases, and especially the time limit for objections to the Guardian Council, are determined by fundamental law.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 8:59â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Article 64

The President guarantees the independence of the Judiciary power, and the Supreme Judicial Council assists him in this regard. The establishment of the judiciary organizations is determined by the fundamental law. The sitting judges are irremovable and cannot be dismissed or transferred.

Ø§ÛŒÙ† ØªØ´ÙƒÛŒÙ„Ø§Øª Ø¯Ø±Ø¨Ø§Ø±Ù‡ Ø¶Ù…Ø§Ù†Øª Ø§Ø¬Ø±Ø§ÛŒÛŒ Ø§Ù†Ø¶Ø¨Ø§Ø·ÛŒ Ù…Ø±Ø¨ÙˆØ· Ø¨Ù‡ Ù‚Ø¶Ø§Øª Ø¯Ø§Ø¯Ø³Ø±Ø§ Ù†Ø¸Ø± Ù…ÛŒâ€ŒØ¯Ù‡Ø¯. Ø±ÛŒØ§Ø³Øª Ø¢Ù† Ø¨Ø§ Ø¯Ø§Ø¯Ø³ØªØ§Ù† ÙƒÙ„ ÙƒØ´ÙˆØ± Ø§Ø³Øª. Ù‚Ø§Ù†ÙˆÙ†ÛŒ Ø³Ø§Ø²Ù…Ø§Ù†ÛŒ
Ø´Ø±Ø§ÛŒØ· Ø§Ø¬Ø±Ø§ÛŒ Ø§ØµÙ„ Ø­Ø§Ø¶Ø± Ø±Ø§ ØªØ¹ÛŒÛŒÙ† Ù…ÛŒ Ù†Ù…Ø§ÛŒØ¯.
ğŸ”¹Article 65

The President guarantees the independence of the Judiciary.
The High Council of the Judiciary assists him in this matter.
The Judiciary is formed in accordance with the Basic Law.
Judges are sitting members and cannot be removed or replaced.

ğŸ”¹Article 65-1

The head of the Supreme Council of Judges is the President. The Minister of Justice is its Vice President according to the law. He can also be the President's deputy.
The Supreme Council of Judges consists of two bodies, one of which is authorized to deal with sitting judges, and the other with judges of the courts.
The competent authority regarding sitting judges, in addition to the President and the Minister of Justice, consists of five sitting judges, one court judge, a government advisor appointed by the Cabinet, and three personalities who are neither members of parliament nor affiliated with the judiciary, appointed respectively by the President, the Speaker of the National Assembly, and the Speaker of the Senate.
The competent authority regarding judges of the courts, in addition to the President and the Minister of Justice, consists of five court judges, one sitting judge, a government advisor, and the three personalities mentioned in the previous paragraph.

ğŸ”¹Article 65-2

The Supreme Council of Judges proposes appointments of sitting judges to the Chief Justice of the Supreme Court, the Head of the State Dispute Resolution Council, and the heads of emergency courts. Other sitting judges are appointed with the favorable opinion of this council.
This body acts as the disciplinary supervisory council for sitting judges. At this time, its chairmanship is with the Chief Justice of the Supreme Court.
The Supreme Council of Judges, with the exception of appointments that are determined by the Council of Ministers, expresses its opinion on the appointment of judges of the courts.
This body also expresses its opinion on the executive discipline guarantee for judges of the courts. The Prosecutor General is the head of this council. An organizational law determines the conditions for the implementation of this principle.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 9:00â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Article 66

No one can be arrested or detained except in accordance with the law. The judiciary, which is the guardian of individual freedoms, is responsible for the enforcement of this principle under the conditions laid down by law.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 9:00â€¯PM]

Ù‚Ø§Ù†ÙˆÙ† Ø¨Ù†ÛŒØ§Ø¯ÛŒØŒ ØªØ±ÙƒÛŒØ¨ Ø¯ÛŒÙˆØ§Ù† Ø¹Ø§Ù„ÛŒØŒ Ø´Ø±Ø­ ÙˆØ¸Ø§ÛŒÙ Ùˆ Ø¢ÛŒÛŒÙ† Ø¯Ø§Ø¯Ø±Ø³ÛŒ Ø¢Ù† Ø±Ø§ Ù…Ø¹ÛŒÙ† Ù…ÛŒ ÙƒÙ†Ø¯.
ğŸ”¹Article 67

A "Supreme Court of Justice" shall be established. The members of the "Supreme Court of Justice" shall be elected by the National Assembly and the Senate from among their own members, in equal numbers, after each general or partial renewal of these Assemblies. The Court shall choose its own President from among its members.

The Fundamental Law shall determine the composition of the Supreme Court, the description of its duties, and its rules of procedure.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 9:00â€¯PM]

Ø±Ø¦ÛŒØ³ Ø¬Ù…Ù‡ÙˆØ± Ø¨Ø±Ø§ÛŒ Ø§Ø¹Ù…Ø§Ù„ Ø§Ù†Ø¬Ø§Ù… ÛŒØ§ÙØªÙ‡ Ø¯Ø± Ø§Ø¬Ø±Ø§ÛŒ ÙˆØ¸Ø§ÛŒÙ Ø®ÙˆÛŒØ´ØŒ Ø¬Ø² Ø¯Ø± ØµÙˆØ±Øª Ø§Ø±ØªÙƒØ§Ø¨ Ø®ÛŒØ§Ù†Øª Ø¨Ù‡ ÙƒØ´ÙˆØ± Ù…Ø³Ø¦ÙˆÙ„ Ù†ÛŒØ³Øª. ğŸ”¹Article 68

The President shall not be responsible for the actions performed in the discharge of his duties, except in cases where he has committed treason against the country. He shall be held accountable only by the two houses of the Parliament by an open vote of the absolute majority of the members of each house and shall be tried by the Supreme Court.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 9:01â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Ø§ØµÙ„ Ø´ØµØª Ùˆ Ù‡Ø´ØªÙ… - Ø¨Ù†Ø¯ Ø³Ù‡

Ù…Ù‚Ø±Ø±Ø§Øª ÙØµÙ„ Ø­Ø§Ø¶Ø± Ù¾ÛŒØ´ Ø§Ø² Ù„Ø§Ø²Ù… Ø§Ù„Ø§Ø¬Ø±Ø§ Ø´Ø¯Ù† Ø¢Ù†ØŒ Ø¯Ø± Ù…ÙˆØ±Ø¯ Ø§Ø¹Ù…Ø§Ù„ Ù…Ø±ØªÙƒØ¨Ù‡ Ù‚Ø§Ø¨Ù„ÛŒØª Ø§Ø¬Ø±Ø§ÛŒÛŒ Ø¯Ø§Ø±Ù†Ø¯.
ğŸ”¹Article 68 - Clause 1

Government officials are responsible for any criminal or tortious acts committed in the course of their duties. They will be tried by the Judiciary of the Islamic Republic of Iran. The Judiciary of the Islamic Republic of Iran is bound by the definitions of crimes and torts, as well as the determination of the penalties resulting from the laws.

ğŸ”¹Article 68 - Clause 2

The Judiciary of the Islamic Republic of Iran consists of fifteen judges: twelve members of parliament, elected by an equal number from the National Assembly and the Senate, after each general or partial renewal of these assemblies, and three judges of the Supreme Court, one of whom presides over the Judiciary of the Islamic Republic of Iran. Anyone who claims to have been harmed by a crime or tort committed by a government official in the course of his duties can file a complaint with an investigative commission. This commission issues an order to enforce the verdict or to refer it to the Prosecutor General of the Supreme Court for referral to the Judiciary of the Islamic Republic of Iran. The Prosecutor General of the Supreme Court may also refer it to the Judiciary of the Islamic Republic of Iran at his discretion with the consent of the investigative commission. The Fundamental Law determines the conditions for the implementation of this article.

ğŸ”¹Article 68 - Clause 3

The provisions of this chapter have executive feasibility in regard to the committed acts before their execution.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 9:03â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹Article 69

The Economic and Social Council declares its opinion on legislative bills, approvals, and legal proposals referred to it by the government, upon its request. One of the members of the Economic and Social Council is elected to declare the council's opinion to the two chambers regarding bills and plans presented to it.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 9:03â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ Article 70
The government can also consult with the "Supreme Council of Economic and Social Affairs" on all issues that have economic and social aspects. Any plan or bill regarding programs that have economic or social aspects will be presented to the council for opinion.

ğŸ”¹ Article 71

The composition of the "Supreme Council of Economic and Social Affairs" and its duties shall be specified by the Basic Law.

ğŸ”¹Article 72
The divisions of the country in the Islamic Republic are provinces and townships. Any other divisions of the country are established by law.
The councils elected by the above-mentioned divisions administer them freely and according to the law.
In the provinces, the representative of the government safeguards national interests, supervises the administration, and ensures compliance with the law.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 9:32â€¯PM]

ğŸ”¹ Article 73

Citizens of the Republic who do not possess the status of civil public rights referred to in Article 34 shall retain their personal legal status until they renounce it.

ğŸ”¹Article 75

The right to revise the Constitution jointly belongs to the President, the Prime Minister, and the members of the Parliament.

The revision bill or proposal must be approved with the same text in both Houses of Parliament. The revision will be definitive through a referendum after its approval.

However, in case the President decides to present the revision bill to the Parliament, which holds a joint session, it will not be put to a general vote; in this case, the revision bill will only be approved by obtaining a majority (three-fifths) of the total votes cast. The joint session office will be the same as that of the National Assembly.

When the territorial integrity of the country is endangered, revising the Constitution or pursuing it is impossible.

The form of the Republican government cannot be subject to revision.

Constitution of Iran, [10/17/22 10:27â€¯PM]
